<div id="review_1079696736" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1079696736" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1079696736?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451150684" href="/book/show/1697775.The_Dead_Zone">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">King fans and fans of politics</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1079696736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1659236146685187320">For Goodreads: 2.5 stars.<br/> <br/>I think I dislike this book a little more every time I read it. The Dead Zone is, for the most part, boring setups that lead to lackluster climaxes, if they can be called climaxes at all. Maybe "payoffs" would be a better word... But I think what I dislike the most about this book is all the political mumbo jumbo. I simply don't give a shit about politics, and this book is full of it. If Johnny Smith isn't thinking about how shitty he has it, he's ruminating on the poli</span>
  <span id="freeText1659236146685187320" style="display:none">For Goodreads: 2.5 stars.<br /> <br />I think I dislike this book a little more every time I read it. The Dead Zone is, for the most part, boring setups that lead to lackluster climaxes, if they can be called climaxes at all. Maybe "payoffs" would be a better word... But I think what I dislike the most about this book is all the political mumbo jumbo. I simply don't give a shit about politics, and this book is full of it. If Johnny Smith isn't thinking about how shitty he has it, he's ruminating on the political climate. This is purely subjective, of course, because if you dig your stories dredged in government, battered in legislature, and fried in policy then this book is definitely for you. <br /> <br />Honestly, The Dead Zone never had a chance. Not this time around at least. Especially coming off my reread of King's exceptional third outing, The Shining. (In case you're wondering, I skipped The Stand because I just reread it last year.) I suppose The Dead Zone is a perfect example of that old saying: They can't all be winners. King came out the gate with five fantastic novels. He was bound to lay a stinker on the world eventually.<br /> <br />I do enjoy the first 140 or so pages of this book, but everything's downhill from there. King had some terrific characters, but it seems as if he didn't really know what do with them once they were established. It's funny, because the book feels more like a collection of interconnected short stories than it does a novel.<br /> <br />Notes on the film and television adaptations: I love Christopher Walken. He's one of my favorite actors. But I've never been able to finish the film adaptation of this book. It bores me to sleep every time. Shit's better than L-tryptophan, son! And the TV series with that dude from Weird Science? All I saw of that were the commercials. I suppose this story just doesn't pique my interest. I do believe this is the final time I'm reading this one. Maybe...<br /> <br />Notable names:<br />Jerusalem's Lot (Obvious)<br />Gendron (used throughout the King-verse)<br />Richard Dees (the despicable main character of King's short story "The Night Flier")<br />Inside View (a gossip rag like The Enquirer that shows up quite bit inside the King-verse. The aforementioned Richard Dees is a headhunter for said magazine.)<br />Carrie (mentioned as a book instead of a person)<br />And, of course, Castle Rock (No-brainer)<br /> <br />In summation: One of my bottom five when it comes to King's books, right down there with Wizard and Glass and the absolutely terrible From a Buick 8. I'm definitely not looking forward to my reread of the latter.<br /> <br />On to Firestarter, which I don't remember at all. I read this one in my teens and haven't read it since. I'm looking forward to it because I don't remember hating it and I dig the movie adaptation very much.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1659236146685187320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16718779910782643825">'If this talent was a gift from God, then God was a dangerous lunatic who ought to be stopped' <br/><br/>When I decided to read all SK works in publication order it was purely because I was told this was the easiest way to spot signs of the multiverse and I think I've found my first cross overs! This book directly mentions Salems Lot and Carrie.   <span id="freeText16718779910782643825" style="display:none">'If this talent was a gift from God, then God was a dangerous lunatic who ought to be stopped' <br /><br />When I decided to read all SK works in publication order it was purely because I was told this was the easiest way to spot signs of the multiverse and I think I've found my first cross overs! This book directly mentions Salems Lot and Carrie. I am of course wondering if I missed any subtle links though so help a girl out if there's others in this book.<br /><br />Another brilliant read from SK! I imagine reading this in the early 80's the character of Stillson would have seemed ridiculous but you can definitely see the parallels between him and Trump. <br /><br />Really loved Johnny Smith, such an all round genuine character that I found so relatable and just rooted for. And Herb, ahhh Herb! <br /><br />I didnt overly love the ending, I'm left with a few unanswered questions but overall I really enjoyed this.<br /><br />Four stars.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5427896789754933977">THE DEAD ZONE was my very first Stephen King book, and I would like to thank David Cronenberg, Christopher Walken, and one of my high school best friends- Natalie Kowalski- for introducing me to the world of John Smith, and in turn the world of Stephen King.<br/><br/><span>[image error]</span><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384267718i/6831287.jpg' alt=' photo 7944f53f-01da-402e-bfc1-0d0e2bc6f0d4_zpsec2f5fa1.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>After watching and falling for the character John Smith- in the 1983 movie THE DEAD ZONE, I decided to search out the book that it was based on.   <span id="freeText5427896789754933977" style="display:none">THE DEAD ZONE was my very first Stephen King book, and I would like to thank David Cronenberg, Christopher Walken, and one of my high school best friends- Natalie Kowalski- for introducing me to the world of John Smith, and in turn the world of Stephen King.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384267718i/6831287.jpg" alt=" photo 7944f53f-01da-402e-bfc1-0d0e2bc6f0d4_zpsec2f5fa1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After watching and falling for the character John Smith- in the 1983 movie THE DEAD ZONE, I decided to search out the book that it was based on. I had never heard of Stephen King- I had read a lot of mysteries, but had never read a horror novel. To me this was the perfect start into the genre. It is suspenseful and gripping without being gory.<br><br>Johnny Smith- is a well liked small-town schoolteacher. After dropping off his first love -Sarah- at her house , he gets into a horrible car accident, which puts him into a coma for five...long...years. When he finally wakes up, everything has changed. Sarah has moved on, his mother is even mooooooore unstable, his father is having a hard time coping with his marriage and hospital bills, and a man called Greg Stillson has entered into the world of politics. Something else is different too- while John has always had an uncanny ability to find lost things or predict small future events, now this "gift" has turned into something much more powerful.<br><br>This will always be one of my favorite Stephen King novels- partly because it was my first, and also because of John Smith and his story- he is certainly a character I have never wanted to let go of. This is my second reading of the book, I watch the movie at least once a year, and I also loved the cheesy -TV USA Network starring Anthony Michael Hall- version of it as well. <br><br><span>[image error]</span><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384267718i/6831288.jpg" alt=" photo 20ab4f78-0191-467e-9b52-a8b0a153bdf6_zpsc2331fe6.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br> <br></span>

<div id="review_75784320" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75784320" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2795921-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528849864p2/2795921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/75784320?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/2795921-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781501144509" href="/book/show/28187208-the-dead-zone">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer75784320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13303286623710756205">The first part of Stephen King’s The Dead Zone was just straight-up fun to read. It had that Something Wicked This Way Comes vibe to it with the spinning wheel, the creepy carnival worker, and Johnny Smith pressing his luck and drawing a crowd. It was the first chapter in what ultimately becomes The Saga of John Smith, Psychic or Something. <br/><br/>The rest of the book walks through events where this psychic ability becomes useful in a number of ways, ultimately leading up to a thrilling, larger-than-li</span>
  <span id="freeText13303286623710756205" style="display:none">The first part of Stephen King’s The Dead Zone was just straight-up fun to read. It had that Something Wicked This Way Comes vibe to it with the spinning wheel, the creepy carnival worker, and Johnny Smith pressing his luck and drawing a crowd. It was the first chapter in what ultimately becomes The Saga of John Smith, Psychic or Something. <br /><br />The rest of the book walks through events where this psychic ability becomes useful in a number of ways, ultimately leading up to a thrilling, larger-than-life climax that puts ole Johnny in a precarious situation with huge stakes, really unbelievable stakes, but, man, when you get there, who even cares anymore? This guys is magical and he’s saving the world!<br /><br />Having multiple plots building on each other was a little awkward at times. I finished one storyline and moved on to the next section, and this time Johnny has landed a new job of living somewhere else, time jumps forward a bit, and those precious events are only mentioned a few times, replaced by something even bigger this time. Johnny’s gotta take his powers to the next level. Time to ditch the minor leagues and show the majors what you can do for once. <br /><br />Mr. King never fails at setting a scene or developing his characters, and his abilities are on full display here as well. Vera, the mother, is a little over the top with her fanatical religious antics, but it’s there for a reason. Sarah and her adventures that become more subplot are drawn up very well and her relationship with Johnny plays out in an interesting, and mostly believable way. The bad guys are bad. There are a few of them around. I loved the small town setting, especially as the political stuff started to kick in later. Hearing King bounce his political views around a bit through the dialogue was a treat. I dig his style. <br /><br />This was certainly a thrilling adventure, and at times it even made me think. If I had that kind of ability, if I could see things happening down the road, how would I handle it? What decisions would I be willing to make? It was cool to read a King book and get myself all mixed up in a wild story, but I also came away thinking about life just a smidge. That doesn’t always happen with this guy. Sometimes it’s vampires and werewolves. Other times it’s dead zones and saving people. <br /><br />Firestarter is next (which my iPhone insists should be two words, so maybe I’m wrong here). I haven’t read that one yet, ever. Looking forward to taking another step on this read-King-books-in-order trail. I’ve never made it this far before, and I’ve got a long way to go, but it’ll be nice to fill in the gaps with books like this one that I skipped in the past or just never got around to. Also, Drew Barrymore. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13303286623710756205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1763728523" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1763728523" />
    <a title="Marchpane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6677659-marchpane"><img alt="Marchpane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483537315p2/6677659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1763728523?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marchpane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marchpane" href="/user/show/6677659-marchpane">Marchpane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340952689" href="/book/show/2395869.The_Dead_Zone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6677659-marchpane?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6677659-marchpane?shelf=big-books">big-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1763728523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13425693056752508886">Most of Stephen King’s famous early novels have an iconic scene (Carrie at the prom), an iconic character (number 1 fan Annie Wilkes) or just a really simple hook (vampires; deserted creepy hotel; zombie pets; killer dog; killer car; killer clown etc… )<br/><br/><i>The Dead Zone</i>, on the other hand, is the one with the ordinary schoolteacher (John Smith, no middle name) who might be a touch psychic, who gets in an accident, ends up in a coma, wakes up from the coma to discover he’s <i>really</i> psychic, avoids usin</span>
  <span id="freeText13425693056752508886" style="display:none">Most of Stephen King’s famous early novels have an iconic scene (Carrie at the prom), an iconic character (number 1 fan Annie Wilkes) or just a really simple hook (vampires; deserted creepy hotel; zombie pets; killer dog; killer car; killer clown etc… )<br /><br /><i>The Dead Zone</i>, on the other hand, is the one with the ordinary schoolteacher (John Smith, no middle name) who might be a touch psychic, who gets in an accident, ends up in a coma, wakes up from the coma to discover he’s <i>really</i> psychic, avoids using this new ability, then (reluctantly) uses it a bit, mostly to save people/property from fires, once (reluctantly) to chase a serial killer, then … eventually … to try to save America and the world from a loose cannon politician. <br /><br />So yeah, it’s baggy and unfocused but I remember being totally engrossed the first time I read this (probably around age 12 or 13). Even minor details and scenes have stuck with me—like the traveling salesman hawking lightning rods at a dusty roadhouse bar. It’s the storytelling. It doesn’t matter that it’s slow and sinuous, that the pacing is uneven, that it’s kind of cheesy, King the Storyteller casts some kind of spell.<br /><br />This re-read was a lot of fun, but something niggled at me. Something felt different since I last read this book. It’s not that it seems dated (it was already dated the first time around) or that I’m a more discerning reader (although I’d like to think so!). Eventually it clicked… <i>11/22/63</i>. I’d read <i>11/22/63</i>.<br /><br />Published 32 years apart, <i>11/22/63</i>—which <b>does</b> have a really simple hook: time travel to save JFK!—and <i>The Dead Zone</i> are like fraternal twins. Both involve political assassinations. One has a psychic who can see the future; the other has a time-traveller <i>from</i> the future. John needs to prevent a fictional disaster; Jake needs to change a real historical event. John aims to preserve our reality; Jake attempts to change it. It’s killing Hitler versus… saving JFK. <br /><br />It’s not like <i>11/22/63</i> is a complete rehash, they’re very different books in many ways. But the similarities that are there make it all the more obvious when these two novels diverge on big questions like ‘can one man be a hero?’ and ‘can you ever cheat fate?’ And it made me see the ending of <i>The Dead Zone</i> in a whole new light.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13425693056752508886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3392998311" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3392998311" />
    <a title="Dennis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64621419-dennis"><img alt="Dennis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604273386p2/64621419.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3392998311?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dennis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dennis" href="/user/show/64621419-dennis">Dennis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Taschenbuch 9783453007048" href="/book/show/2720360-dead-zone-das-attentat">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64621419-dennis?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64621419-dennis?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3392998311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17057990858001020859">Stephen and I we have the most curious relationship.<br/><br/>I've got this list of Stephen King novels that make me beg to please let me die already, because of all of this time he takes to build his characters and their backstories, going into every minor detail of seemingly every experience they make, no matter how inconsequential they may seem to be for the plot. I also have this other list of Stephen King novels. The ones I adore, because of all of this time he takes to build his characters and their</span>
  <span id="freeText17057990858001020859" style="display:none">Stephen and I we have the most curious relationship.<br /><br />I've got this list of Stephen King novels that make me beg to please let me die already, because of all of this time he takes to build his characters and their backstories, going into every minor detail of seemingly every experience they make, no matter how inconsequential they may seem to be for the plot. I also have this other list of Stephen King novels. The ones I adore, because of all of this time he takes to build his characters and their backstories, going into every minor detail of seemingly every experience they make, no matter how inconsequential they may seem to be for the plot. Sometimes I almost think it simply comes down to pure luck, or maybe timing, whether I like his books or not. Sure, there’s also this third group of books, those in which he is also waffling endlessly, but with no pay-off whatsoever. Or at least none that I am capable of seeing. But most of the time his books will land in one of the two categories above, where I can appreciate him as a writer and, for pretty much the same reasons, either love or hate the book.<br /><br />This one here falls squarely on the positive side of the spectrum. Like pretty much every King novel it requires patience. But the story of a man that, in the prime of his life, has a tragic accident, spends years in a coma, wakes from said coma when almost everyone had given up hope, discovers that he now possesses a gift for knowing things about people by simply touching them, which soon turns into a burden as he tries to fight his way back into life, this story comes with a pay-off. It took its time to draw me in, sure. But there was still a lot of story left when I very much started to feel for Johnny, feared for what was going to happen to him, became curious about when and how he would cross paths with the other main character.<br /><br />This other main character is a ruthlessly opportunistic politician that has a knack for entertaining the masses, and also a program that includes shooting garbage bags to Mars in order to solve the problem of pollution. Yes, he did indeed remind me of another <s>clown</s> politician, just like people had told me he would.<br /><br />There’s also a side-plot about a serial killer, that makes Johnny turn up in Castle Rock, and a lot of (at the time) contemporary topics that King touches upon. It was a very immersive experience. And while I don’t feel quite the same love for it that I feel for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/830502.It" title="It by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener"> It</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107291.Needful_Things" title="Needful Things by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener"> Needful Things</a>, it was definitely very rewarding and a highly enjoyable read.<br /><br /><i>A buddy read with the Stephen King Readers in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">SpecFic</a> to be precise. Thanks, guys! It was fun.</i><br /><br />Up next in my already failed attempt to read all the stories set in Castle Rock, before I will read Needful Things: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10603.Cujo" title="Cujo by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener"> Cujo</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17057990858001020859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11676151803304655769">John Smith's life was going good. He loved his job teaching, he was good at it, and the kids really liked having him for a teacher. He was in love with his girlfriend, Sara, a fellow teacher. They were going to the county fair and Sarah asked him to spend the night. He had a very strange run of luck guessing what numbers would come up on the wheel at the fair, in fact Sara was frightened by the way he looked as he won round after round. She started to get sick, maybe from a bad hot dog, so Johnn</span>
  <span id="freeText11676151803304655769" style="display:none">John Smith's life was going good. He loved his job teaching, he was good at it, and the kids really liked having him for a teacher. He was in love with his girlfriend, Sara, a fellow teacher. They were going to the county fair and Sarah asked him to spend the night. He had a very strange run of luck guessing what numbers would come up on the wheel at the fair, in fact Sara was frightened by the way he looked as he won round after round. She started to get sick, maybe from a bad hot dog, so Johnny ended up taking a cab home, instead of spending the night. He never made it home. The last thing Johnny remembered was the cab crashing head-on into another car. He didn't wake up again for 4 and a half years and when he did, he found that he had gained the gift or curse, however you want to look at it, of psychic powers when he touched someone or something.<br />The Dead Zone is one of Stephen King's best books in my opinion. It's a paranormal rather than horror story and John Smith is a very sympathetic hero. The reason he was given the powers comes when he shakes the hand of a politician named Ed Stillson.<br />I highly recommend this book, even to those who normally don't like Stephen King. This was the first Reading For Pleasure Terror Tribe Buddy Read and it was a fantastic choice.<br />I listened to an audiobook from Overdrive narrated by James Franco, who did an excellent job.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9284671679580100740">I have the film adaptation of this on VHS (it's one of my few tapes I haven't watched yet), and reading <i>The Dead Zone</i> really makes me want to watch it now. As is often the case in King's books, the characters have supernatural powers, but something about John Smith's abilities stand out high above those of Charlie McGee's pyrokinesis. King focuses less on shady people who want to use this power for evil, and more on John Smith himself and what his own conscience is telling him to do.<br/><br/>I can defini</span>
  <span id="freeText9284671679580100740" style="display:none">I have the film adaptation of this on VHS (it's one of my few tapes I haven't watched yet), and reading <i>The Dead Zone</i> really makes me want to watch it now. As is often the case in King's books, the characters have supernatural powers, but something about John Smith's abilities stand out high above those of Charlie McGee's pyrokinesis. King focuses less on shady people who want to use this power for evil, and more on John Smith himself and what his own conscience is telling him to do.<br /><br />I can definitely see why David Cronenberg, who brought us the amazing works <i>Scanners</i> and <i>The Fly</i>, would want to adapt <i>The Dead Zone</i>. This is a very powerful story and it has an unforgettable way of holding up human nature to the wonder of the supernatural and remarkable. It begs the question for all readers, if you had special powers, what would you use them for? If you knew something bad was coming, what would you do? This book isn't all dark and serious, of course. King injects his own brand of subtle humor into the characters and dialogue throughout, and there's also some time for a bit of drama.</span>

<div id="review_1062121091" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1062121091" />
    <a title="Paul Nelson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7553206-paul-nelson"><img alt="Paul Nelson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434048386p2/7553206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1062121091?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Nelson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Nelson" href="/user/show/7553206-paul-nelson">Paul Nelson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7553206-paul-nelson?shelf=2014-books-read">2014-books-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1062121091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9360078153380572761">Next up on my Stephen King quest is The Dead Zone, again it’s not a review as such but a collection of my thoughts on the book. So there may well be spoilers but I think pretty much everyone has read it a long time ago anyway, all except me.<br/><br/>After reading The Stand & Salem’s Lot in quick succession, you start to appreciate what a spellbinding storyteller The King can be and I can compare these to the other end of the spectrum, his newly released material, Mr Mercedes & Doctor Sleep. The outstandi</span>
  <span id="freeText9360078153380572761" style="display:none">Next up on my Stephen King quest is The Dead Zone, again it’s not a review as such but a collection of my thoughts on the book. So there may well be spoilers but I think pretty much everyone has read it a long time ago anyway, all except me.<br /><br />After reading The Stand &amp; Salem’s Lot in quick succession, you start to appreciate what a spellbinding storyteller The King can be and I can compare these to the other end of the spectrum, his newly released material, Mr Mercedes &amp; Doctor Sleep. The outstanding feature in his new material is the depth he gives to his characters, a depth that was touched on but not prevalent at the start of his career. His new stuff wraps the art of storytelling neatly into a bundle, with gripping characterization and plots that leave you hanging on for more.<br /><br />The Dead Zone sort of explores Stephen King’s development as a skilled author, in this book he shows that his characters are becoming more deeply fleshed out than previous works but in my opinion he loses his way with the story a little, concentrating more on one aspect of the story and dropping the ball in others.<br /><br />I did enjoy the story of Jonny Smith, he is a character that is easy to invest everything in but my problem lay with the bad guys. They simply weren’t in the story enough to get any feel for, There was a chapter about the killer early on and then nothing more until he was identified, which was a little too easy, there should have been more airtime devoted to the killer to ramp up the tension, no reveal but more focus around his acts themselves. <br /><br />Then we have Greg Stillson who for me just wasn’t a worthy bad guy for the end play, truthfully I couldn’t give a flying fuck what happened to him and Jonny’s mission to kill the guy seemed almost meaningless to me. I appreciate he saw him becoming President and heralding a nuclear war but I was more taken in by Jonny and his teaching successes with Chuck, the lightning strike and his relationship with Sarah than I was with how the book ended.<br /><br />I know this book is well thought of by most, even a favourite but for me it was a case of the writer honing his considerable talents for future forays, primarily a character driven story that sacrificed plot devices that when I think back could have been made a classic so easily by simply veering slightly off the path he set for himself.<br /><br />Anyway that’s just my opinion and I guess most wouldn’t wholeheartedly agree with it but it’s my Stephen King trip and that’s how I see it.<br /><br />So that’s 16 completed from my target of 66 books and a nice round 50 to go, a fair undertaking I think you’ll agree.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://paulnelson.booklikes.com/post/1032864/the-dead-zone-by-stephen-king">http://paulnelson.booklikes.com/post/...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9360078153380572761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_839712030" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer839712030" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer221526432289922789">January 2016-<br/>Oh man! I totally read this book in January of 2014! I even wrote that in the book so I wouldn't forget. I mean, the minute I read the prologue, I knew I had read it recently. Johnny Smith, falls down ice skating and his world is never the same again. How can I forget that I read this? It wasn't even that long ago-two(ish) years ago?<br/>So let me give more of a review though:<br/>This is one of King's greatest character developments. The protagonist is someone we find ourselves very connecte</span>
  <span id="freeText221526432289922789" style="display:none">January 2016-<br />Oh man! I totally read this book in January of 2014! I even wrote that in the book so I wouldn't forget. I mean, the minute I read the prologue, I knew I had read it recently. Johnny Smith, falls down ice skating and his world is never the same again. How can I forget that I read this? It wasn't even that long ago-two(ish) years ago?<br />So let me give more of a review though:<br />This is one of King's greatest character developments. The protagonist is someone we find ourselves very connected to, very invested in his story. We want John to do well. <br />In hindsight, I wonder if Stephen King used this earlier novel to influence his story Revival? They remind me of each other with the intersecting/connected lives of John and Stillson. Also, there is that incident with lightening--remember that? Super familiar.<br />I love the ending too-bringing it full circle with the love interest, Sarah.<br />A great read from the Master!<br /><br />Update Fe. 25th, 2019 #reviewking2019 project-revisiting old Stephen King reviews:<br />So first of all, I browsed through the book today and wound up re-reading whole portions of it. I'm amazed by the fact that so often, I see people talking about Jake &amp; Sadie as King's most romantic couple, or even Roland and Susan but have we forgotten Johnny and Sarah from The Dead Zone? Because I really, really like Johnny. He might be one of King's most healthy protagonists.<br />I love how midway through the book, we get this Spiderman-esque plot line where Johnny (due to an unfortunate accident and coma, he wakes up with a supernatural ability) gets to use his newly developed "powers" to help local authorities catch a serial killer. Johnny isn't a Batman like hero--taking to the streets to solve crime, but more like the reluctant hero we see in Spiderman but told with all the talent Stephen King brings to the table and it's so compelling!!<br />But enough about the protagonist--what about our antagonist, Greg Stillson-who for all intents and purposes reminds me so much of our current POTUS (he who shall not be named but who always says stupid things like "fake news").<br />Greg Stillson is evil, evil, EVIL and our favorite protagonist, Johnny is the man to stop his rise to power.<br />I love the ending of this book and I enjoyed re-reading it today before I wrote this review. Seriously, this could make its way onto my top 10 list.<br />It's worthy. I changed my review from 4 stars to 5.<br />And legendary being that it's the first Castle Rock book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="221526432289922789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14026249630676933411">1.25 stars<br/><b>DNF @89%</b><br/><br/>Me at the moment:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464365459ra/19232334.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>The Dead Zone</i> is my least favorite Stephen King novel so far. I genuinely didn't like it at best, really hated it at worst. I thought it was boring, in-comprehensive, and bland. <b>The main story centers aroudn Johnny Smith, your average ya-hoo, who happened to get himself into an accident and (after 4.5 years in a coma) wakes up to find himself being a seer.</b> Interesting enough set-up. Unfortunately, the book becomes a mess after these first chapters. <br/><br/>First, I'd l</span>
  <span id="freeText14026249630676933411" style="display:none">1.25 stars<br><b>DNF @89%</b><br><br>Me at the moment:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464365459ra/19232334.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>The Dead Zone</i> is my least favorite Stephen King novel so far. I genuinely didn't like it at best, really hated it at worst. I thought it was boring, in-comprehensive, and bland. <b>The main story centers aroudn Johnny Smith, your average ya-hoo, who happened to get himself into an accident and (after 4.5 years in a coma) wakes up to find himself being a seer.</b> Interesting enough set-up. Unfortunately, the book becomes a mess after these first chapters. <br><br>First, I'd like to challenge myself to find one element of this story that I actually enjoyed... after all, I did give it a .25 star bonus right? <b>The one ok segment of the book is the series of events leading up to the accident.</b> I thoroughly enjoyed Johnny and Sarah, the ice-skating in the first chapter transported me to my memories of ice-skating. King did something that I didn't see in his works yet: he made it fairy-tale like for just a few paragraphs and it was magical. Heck, even the first chapter after the accident that follows Sarah and his family getting used to the fact that Johnny is hurt was good. I wish I could say more good about <i>The Dead Zone</i>, but I can't.<br><br>The question this book poses is "if you could go back in time and kill Hitler, would you?". For a few brief scenes about a man named Greg Stillson who is running for president. He is the main antagonist of the story from what I could tell (and from what I read on the wikipedia summary of the last 50 pages that I didn't read). From what I understood, these scenes with him are supposed to be foreshadowing for future events or parallels. I think if King played this part up, I would have enjoyed this more. Instead, <b>you get a side plot about a serial killer (resolved in some 3-4 chapter), a side plot about a kid who can't read (another 3-4 chapters), a whole bunch of King trying to add depth to Johnny while maintaining him as a good-innocent-type guy</b> (kind of like his character Stu Redman from <i>The Stand</i> but not at all like Stu Redman). IT WAS SO POINTLESS. At some point I just gave up getting excited when a new conflict came up because I knew that it would be solved in 20 pages. <b>Other than the subtle political undertones, I'd say this book is pretty useless (at least to me). </b><br><br>In the end, I guess I can take inspiration from a character called Lightsong from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1268479.Warbreaker__Warbreaker___1_" title="Warbreaker (Warbreaker, #1) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Warbreaker</a> when formulating my opinion on this book: <b>very drawn out, sharp as hell but lacking a point. </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500398582ra/23334309.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thank you all for joining in for Episode 3 of Quickie Review with Valliya!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1599763132ra/30089160.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Previous episode</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3539457174" rel="nofollow noopener">Sharp Objects</a> - Gillian Flynn ★★★<br><br><b>Next episode</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3582581372" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadows for Silence in the Forests of Hell</a> - Brandon Sanderson ★★.75</span>

<div id="review_2975992969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2975992969" />
    <a title="Michael Jandrok" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66672731-michael-jandrok"><img alt="Michael Jandrok" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561055227p2/66672731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2975992969?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Jandrok" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Jandrok" href="/user/show/66672731-michael-jandrok">Michael Jandrok</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451093387" href="/book/show/13445.The_Dead_Zone">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2975992969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12030756987388165701">Some time last year I decided that it would be a fun idea to reread a lot of the Stephen King canon, starting with his first novel, “Carrie” and then keeping to a more or less chronological schedule, adding in stuff like “The Dead Zone” and “Firestarter” that I had skipped back in the day for whatever unknown reason. I got as far as “The Shining” when I realized that I needed to get off track and knuckle down on “Doctor Sleep,” King’s 2013 sequel to the original and find out what happened to the</span>
  <span id="freeText12030756987388165701" style="display:none">Some time last year I decided that it would be a fun idea to reread a lot of the Stephen King canon, starting with his first novel, “Carrie” and then keeping to a more or less chronological schedule, adding in stuff like “The Dead Zone” and “Firestarter” that I had skipped back in the day for whatever unknown reason. I got as far as “The Shining” when I realized that I needed to get off track and knuckle down on “Doctor Sleep,” King’s 2013 sequel to the original and find out what happened to the remains of the Torrance family after the ashes of the Overlook Hotel cooled. I had also skipped out on “The Stand,” but I expect to correct that later this year. Which brings me back full circle to “The Dead Zone.” First published in 1979, it was the first of King’s books to eschew outright supernatural horror in favor of a toned-down study of the paranormal, in this case the psychic ability to foretell the future. Psychics were still big business back in 1979. Edgar Cayce was always good story fodder for the tabloids and Uri Geller was still bending spoons for talk show hosts, so it shouldn’t have been a surprise to see a writer of King’s stature tackle the subject as a main plot point. <br /><br />King’s tale revolves around one Johnny (no middle name) Smith, a recently minted schoolteacher in a ubiquitous Maine town back in the halcyon days of 1970. Johnny is doing well as a second-year teacher, and manages to catch the eye of one of his rookie teaching cohorts, Sarah Bracknell, and the two head out for a date at the county fair. They have fun and are just about to head home when Johnny is talked into playing a rickety-looking Wheel of Fortune game, where he first displays a taste of his abilities by going on an unprecedented winning streak and winning over $500. Sarah, who has been brought down by a bad country fair hot dog, manages to get herself and Johnny extracted from the fair, at which point he leaves her at her apartment and decides to take a cab back to his place. Which turns out to be not such a swift move, as Johnny and the cab get into a massive road accident that leaves Johnny in a coma for the next four and a half years…….<br /><br />CUT TO…...the backstory, where one Greg Stillson is first encountered while selling Bibles in the midwest. Stillson doesn’t sell any Bibles in this scene, but he does manage to kick a family dog to death, which gives you all you really need to know about Mr. Stillson. He is a driven man, and driven men can also be dangerous men, and Stillson has his sights set high. Just how high, he doesn’t know yet, but it’s clear that he is destined to do bigly things...YUGE things…..<br /><br />Sarah has married during the time that Johnny was in his coma. His mother has gone into deeper and deeper levels of religious paranoia, his father is happy to see him alive and conscious, but is weighed down by guilt from wishing so hard for Johnny’s death during his long ordeal. Johnny himself is a physical and emotional wreck, made worse by the fact that his latent psychic abilities seem to have been honed and enhanced by his brush with death. Johnny need do nothing but touch a person or object to gain an “impression” of it, and this “talent” soon becomes a curse, as Johnny fights his way through several media firestorms in the wake of highly publicized psychic events, one of which leads to the solution of a series of sex crimes. <br /><br />Greg Stillson, meanwhile, has managed to get himself elected to Mayor of his small town, and has set his goal on reaching the House of Representatives. Johnny has become something of a political junkie and manages to make it to one of Stillson’s rallies, where he shakes hands with the candidate and sees a horrible future in store for the human race should Stillson achieve the impossible and get himself elected as POTUS. This is a pretty complex plot, and I’m leaving a lot out, but if you feel a need for a higher level of detail, you can always access the Wiki page for the book:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Dead_Zone_(novel)">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Dea...</a><br /><br />The real action of the book now takes place as the two plotlines converge and Johnny makes a fateful decision on what he must do with the information that he has been given……<br /><br />So…..observations…..I’ll start with the obvious one and riff on the odd similarities between the character of one Greg Stillson and one Donald J.Trump. Stillson is an obvious psychopath who is willing to do whatever it takes to squirm his way up the political ladder. Lies, graft, murder….nothing is off of the table for Stillson. His political rallies are pure theater, meant to entertain the cult of personality and stroke the ego of the man himself. It’s nationalism and populism at its finest, and it won’t be surprising when a substantial portion of the public eats it up like candy. The parallels between Stillson and Trump are obvious in today’s political climate, but for King to have been so spot-on with his characterizations here is a bit spooky. This book was written 40 YEARS AGO. Maybe King HIMSELF has just a bit on that ol’ shine about him…..<br /><br />And speaking of that particular “shine”.......precognition was a minor part of the talents that Danny Torrance evidenced in “The Shining,” but it seems clear to me that this is merely a matter of scale. Johnny’s ability to see the future is just one aspect of the “shining” phenomenon as a whole…..I would put Carrie White’s abilities in that box as well, and possibly even Charlene McGee’s pyrotechnic skills, though a lot of the credit in her case appears to revolve around the drug tests performed on her father. Still, it’s interesting to me that Stephen King seems to be linking a wide range of what we would call “psychic” phenomena under one more or less umbrella term that can take it all in and make contextual sense out of it, a sort of field-unification theory for the expansion of the mind’s more extreme potentialities. <br /><br />I was also highly amused by the peppering of references to Ray Bradbury’s seminal horror novel “Something Wicked This Way Comes.” There are several points in the text that hark back to Bradbury’s vision, one of which is a direct reference to the title itself, and the other a delicious and short chapter dedicated to the “lightning-rod salesman.” I chortled heartily as I read this chapter, and as soon as I was done with it I knew that the storm was gonna COME, baby...bringing lightning bolts of righteous retribution with it. And I was pretty much right. <br /><br />King also manages to throw himself a bone in the text, as one of the characters references “Carrie” at one particularly frightening juncture of the novel. King has always loved including these little easter-eggs in his text, and I never fail to find the fun in picking them up along the way.<br /><br />King was riffing HARD in these early novels, and he gets through “The Dead Zone” in a perilously efficient and powerful 402 pages. His characters are strongly developed and his pacing is just about perfect. “The Dead Zone” was the first of his books to make the yearly Top 10 lists in popularity and sales, and he was just hitting his commercial stride. In that sense, I found it interesting that he would abandon traditional horror in favor of a more subtle treatise on such tabloid fare as “psychics.” But I think he knew his audience well, because those same people buying “The National Enquirer” and “Weekly World News” and reading the daily horoscopes were the same ones that were snapping up copies of his books in the check-out lines of supermarkets across America. All of which makes me think that King is one of the most outstanding observers of human nature EVER, and certainly one of the canniest when it comes down to marketing his material. <br /><br />Bottom line, “The Dead Zone” is a damn fine thriller, and a worthy addition to the King canon. I’m reserving 5 stars for those King books that were clearly head and shoulders above anything like them, but this is a solid 4 star effort and should be recognized as such. This is King in his supercharged youth, cranking out shimmering prose while the crank was yet to impair him. I have no idea why I shunted it aside when I was younger, but I’m glad that I took the time now to correct that unfortunate fact. Now perhaps on to “The Stand”...............</span>
  <a data-text-id="12030756987388165701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3269143227" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3269143227" />
    <a title="Gary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15055195-gary"><img alt="Gary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354386194p2/15055195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3269143227?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary" href="/user/show/15055195-gary">Gary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28254557-the-dead-zone">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3269143227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2167838328046029361">I have had this book on my to read list for so long and finally decided to take the plunge. I had watched the film many years ago and maybe that was why the book didn't quite grip me the way the film did. The premise of the book where a man who wakes up from a five-year coma and is able to see the future and past of people he touches is certainly fascinating and opens a lot of avenues for the author to explore. The story is laid out well and there are some good characters but the book didn't qui</span>
  <span id="freeText2167838328046029361" style="display:none">I have had this book on my to read list for so long and finally decided to take the plunge. I had watched the film many years ago and maybe that was why the book didn't quite grip me the way the film did. The premise of the book where a man who wakes up from a five-year coma and is able to see the future and past of people he touches is certainly fascinating and opens a lot of avenues for the author to explore. The story is laid out well and there are some good characters but the book didn't quite hold me in the same way that 11/22/63 did. Like I said previously because I had already seen the film there were no surprises and some of the magic was probably lost because of that.<br />I have recently acquired many of Stephen King's books as I do enjoy his writing and intend to read a few more throughout the year. This one was slightly disappointing much of it due to my own high expectations. Still a good book and certainly deserves a 3 to 4 star rating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2167838328046029361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2321432860" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2321432860" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57725883-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557030750p2/57725883.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2321432860?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/57725883-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/7593244-the-dead-zone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57725883-rob?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57725883-rob?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2321432860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1168598009304343997">A paranormal thriller form Stephen King published 1979.<br/><br/>4 star excellence.<br/>This is a book that has been kicking around my place for years. A book I promised myself that I’d get round to one of these days. Then after reading some glowing reviews on GR I thought now is the time.<br/><br/>It turned out be a great read.<br/><br/>On this occasion SK delves into one of his favourite topics, the latent power of the human brain. <br/>After two accidents, one minor and the other serious, Johnny Smith ends up in a coma, a coma that</span>
  <span id="freeText1168598009304343997" style="display:none">A paranormal thriller form Stephen King published 1979.<br /><br />4 star excellence.<br />This is a book that has been kicking around my place for years. A book I promised myself that I’d get round to one of these days. Then after reading some glowing reviews on GR I thought now is the time.<br /><br />It turned out be a great read.<br /><br />On this occasion SK delves into one of his favourite topics, the latent power of the human brain. <br />After two accidents, one minor and the other serious, Johnny Smith ends up in a coma, a coma that lasted five years. Doctors never expected Johnny to regain consciousness but much to everyone’s astonishment he did. <br />Along with consciousness Johnny found he had an unwelcome guest inside his head.<br />At times when Johnny had physical contact with someone he would have a flash view into that person’s future. This was all well and good when the outcome was to that person’s advantage. But on one occasion when Johnny shook the hand of the man who was standing for election in the House of Representatives Johnny knew this man was pure evil and needed to be stopped before his career went any further.<br /><br />Watching Johnny Smith’s life unravel as he comes to terms of what he needs to do makes for mesmerising reading. <br />SK does this so well, getting the reader to climb inside the characters head, to point where you feel like you live there. You feel the remorse, the anxiety, the yearning to be understood but above all the desire to be normal.<br /><br />This was a truly fantastic read. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1168598009304343997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_234635086" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/234635086" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6504379-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590065910p2/6504379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/234635086?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/6504379-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451093387" href="/book/show/13445.The_Dead_Zone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=stephen-king-read">stephen-king-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=scifi-fantasy">scifi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=i-recommend">i-recommend</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer234635086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11461773031802286792">What comes from knowing things? Nothing. What is the purpose of knowing the future? So you can change it? But wouldn't what you knew about the future and the change you were going to bring to the future, be the way it was supposed to be anyways? Just think about it...<br/><br/>I think in the case of Johnny Smith and <i>
  <b>The Dead Zone</b>
</i>, I would have to say what happened to Johnny and the events surrounding him, happened for a reason. <br/><br/>This is not a horror novel, in my opinion. This is more of a sci-fi novel </span>
  <span id="freeText11461773031802286792" style="display:none">What comes from knowing things? Nothing. What is the purpose of knowing the future? So you can change it? But wouldn't what you knew about the future and the change you were going to bring to the future, be the way it was supposed to be anyways? Just think about it...<br /><br />I think in the case of Johnny Smith and <i>
  <b>The Dead Zone</b>
</i>, I would have to say what happened to Johnny and the events surrounding him, happened for a reason. <br /><br />This is not a horror novel, in my opinion. This is more of a sci-fi novel done in King-style. I have been really surprised, especially as I read <i>
  <b>The Dead Zone</b>
</i>, this isn't more of a popular read, especially with King readers. Johnny Smith's character and his ability were done very well. I really liked all of the characters, especially Johnny and his parents. <br /><br />About halfway through the novel, I felt like something else was going on, and it turns out I was quite wrong: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I thought the killings were Johnny while he was in the dead zone, because he seemed to not really know what was happening to him while he was there. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I'm glad King made me think one way, and had it turn out to be something else. Mainly because, if it had been what I originally thought, it would have just been too easy for King. <br /><br />My favorite part of the book would have to have been when the killings were going on, and Johnny's role in the particular part. Having just finished the book, that is not a spoiler, and doesn't give away 99.99% of anything which happens within these pages. <br /><br />I really like sci-fi, but only if it is realistic, and is done like <i>
  <b>The Dead Zone</b>
</i>. I'm really happy King penned this novel, and didn't take it to certain lengths I thought it might go. <br /><br />Great job, King! </span>
  <a data-text-id="11461773031802286792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pJSjENalAbEixLIBj5+da+1RS6x6BzXccg4Z2y7MaZIxktqbghFque3yaywto7c7AzJ1zZuIWuhcFtJWJdzFzQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gVdbQL8eibln05zMlSCxx11S1pFzXCIWhw/UXcjDPboUUSLL66risajlReE3HJuXszHo8JLTTSKpFx/Qw9OR5Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Louis recounts how he became a vampire at the hands of the radiant and sinister Lestat and how he became indoctrinated, unwillingly, into the vampire way of life. His story ebbs and flows through the streets of New Orleans, defining crucial moments such as his discovery of the exquisite lost young child Claudia, wanting not to hurt but to comfort her with the last breaths of humanity he has inside. Yet, he makes Claudia a vampire, trapping her womanly passion, will, and intelligence inside the body of a small child. Louis and Claudia form a seemingly unbreakable alliance and even &quot;settle down&quot; for a while in the opulent French Quarter. Louis remembers Claudia\'s struggle to understand herself and the hatred they both have for Lestat that sends them halfway across the world to seek others of their kind. Louis and Claudia are desperate to find somewhere they belong, to find others who understand, and someone who knows what and why they are.\n\nLouis and Claudia travel Europe, eventually coming to Paris and the ragingly successful Theatre des Vampires--a theatre of vampires pretending to be mortals pretending to be vampires. Here they meet the magnetic and ethereal Armand, who brings them into a whole society of vampires. But Louis and Claudia find that finding others like themselves provides no easy answers and in fact presents dangers they scarcely imagined.\n\nOriginally begun as a short story, the book took off as Anne wrote it, spinning the tragic and triumphant life experiences of a soul. As well as the struggles of its characters, Interview captures the political and social changes of two continents. The novel also introduces Lestat, Anne\'s most enduring character, a heady mixture of attraction and revulsion.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4865736111144164819">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText4865736111144164819" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4865736111144164819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
